    "the hydrodynamics of conducting fluids is of great importance in many terrestrial and astrophysical phenomena .",
    "examples include the generation of magnetic fields via dynamo action in the interstellar medium , stars , and planets  @xcite , and liquid - metal systems  @xcite that are studied in laboratories .",
    "the flows in such settings , which can be described at the simplest level by the equations of magnetohydrodynamics ( mhd ) , are often turbulent  @xcite .",
    "the larger the kinetic and magnetic reynolds numbers , @xmath3 and @xmath4 , respectively , the more turbulent is the motion of the conducting fluid ; here @xmath5 and @xmath6 are typical length and velocity scales in the flow , @xmath7 is the kinematic viscosity , and @xmath8 is the magnetic diffusivity .",
    "the statistical characterization of turbulent mhd flows , which continues to pose challenges for experiments  @xcite , direct numerical simulations  @xcite , and theory  @xcite , is even harder than its analogue in fluid turbulence because ( a ) we must control both @xmath9 and @xmath10 and ( b ) we must obtain the statistical properties of both velocity and magnetic fields .",
    "the kinematic viscosity @xmath7 and the magnetic diffusivity @xmath8 can differ by several orders of magnitude , so the magnetic prandtl number @xmath11 can vary over a large range . for example , @xmath12 in the liquid - sodium system  @xcite , @xmath13 at the base of the sun s convection zone  @xcite , and @xmath14 in the interstellar medium  @xcite .",
    "furthermore , two dissipative scales play an important role in mhd ; they are the kolmogorov scale @xmath15 ( @xmath16 at the level of kolmogorov 1941 ( k41 ) phenomenology  @xcite ) and the magnetic - resistive scale @xmath17 ( @xmath18 in k41 )",
    ". a thorough study of the statistical properties of mhd turbulence must resolve both these dissipative scales .",
    "given current computational resources , this is a daunting task at large @xmath19 especially if @xmath1 is significantly different from unity .",
    "thus , most direct numerical simulations ( dns ) of mhd turbulence  @xcite have been restricted to @xmath20 .",
    "some dns studies have now started moving away from the @xmath20 regime especially in the context of the dynamo problem  @xcite .    here",
    "we initiate a detailed dns study of the statistical properties of incompressible , homogeneous , and isotropic mhd turbulence for a large range of the magnetic prandtl number , namely , @xmath2 .",
    "there is no mean magnetic field in our dns  @xcite ; and we restrict ourselves to eulerian measurements  @xcite . before we give the details of our dns study , we highlight a few of our qualitative , principal results .",
    "elements of some of our results , for the case @xmath21 and for quantities such as energy spectra , exist in the mhd - turbulence literature as can be seen from the representative refs .",
    "however , to the best of our knowledge , no study has attempted as detailed and systematic an investigation of the statistical properties of mhd turbulence as we present here , especially with a view to elucidating their dependence on @xmath1 .",
    "our study uncovers interesting trends that have not been noted hitherto .",
    "these emerge from our detailed characterisation of intermittency , via a variety of measures which include various probability distribution functions ( pdfs ) such as those of the modulus of the vorticity and the energy dissipation rates , velocity and magnetic - field structure functions that can be used to characterise intermittency , isosurfaces of quantities such as the moduli of the vorticity and current , and joint pdfs such as those of fluid and magnetic dissipation rates .",
    "earlier dns studies  @xcite have suggested that intermittency , as characterised say by the multiscaling exponents for velocity- and magentic - field structure functions , is more intense for the magnetic field than for the velocity field when @xmath22 .",
    "our study confirms this and suggests , in addition , that this result is reversed as we lower @xmath1 .",
    "this crossover from larger intermittency in the magnetic field than in the velocity field , at large @xmath1 , to smaller intermittency in the magnetic field than in the velocity field , at low @xmath23 , shows up not only in the values of multiscaling exponent ratios , which we obtain from a detailed local - slope analysis of extended - self - similarity ( ess ) plots  @xcite of one structure function against another , but also in the behaviours of tails of pdfs of dissipation rates , the moduli of vorticity and current density , and velocity and magnetic - field increments .",
    "furthermore , a comparison of our results for decaying mhd turbulence and its forced , statistically steady analogue suggest that , at least given our conservative errors , the homogeneous , isotropic mhd turbulence that we study here displays strong universality  @xcite in the sense that multiscaling exponent ratios agree for both decaying and statistically steady cases .",
    "the remaining part of this paper is organised as follows . in sec .",
    "[ sec : equations ] we describe the mhd equations , the details of the numerical schemes we use ( subsection  [ sec : dns ] ) , and the statistical measures we use to characterise mhd turbulence ( subsection  [ sec : statmeasures ] ) . in sec .",
    "[ sec : results ] we present our results ; these are described in the seven subsections  [ sec : ns ] , [ sec : tseries ] , [ sec : spectra ] , [ sec : pdfs ] , [ sec : stfn ] , [ sec : isosurf ] , and [ sec : jpdf ] that are devoted , respectively , to ( a ) a summary of well - known results from fluid turbulence that are relevant to our study , ( b ) the temporal evolution of quantities such as the energy and energy - dissipation rates , ( c ) energy , dissipation - rate , elssser - variable , and effective - pressure spectra , ( d ) various probability distribution functions ( pdfs ) that can be used , _",
    "inter alia _ , to characterise the alignments of vectors such as the vorticity with , say , the eigenvectors of the rate - of - strain tensor , ( e ) velocity and magnetic - field structure functions that can be used to characterise intermittency , ( f ) isosurfaces of quantities such as the moduli of the vorticity and current , and ( g ) and joint pdfs such as those of fluid and magnetic dissipation rates .",
    "section  [ sec : conclusions ] contains a discussion of our results .",

    "the zero - discriminant line @xmath149 and the @xmath150 and @xmath151 axes divide the @xmath152 plane into qualitatively different regimes .",
    "in particular , regions in a turbulent flow can be classified as follows : when @xmath150 is large and negative , local strains are high and vortex formation is not favoured ; furthermore , if @xmath153 , fluid elements experience axial strain , whereas , if @xmath154 , they feel biaxial strain . in contrast ,",
    "when @xmath150 is large and positive , vorticity dominates the flow ; if , in addition , @xmath154 , vortices are compressed , whereas , if @xmath153 , they are stretched . thus , some properties of a turbulent flow can be highlighted by making contour plots of the joint pdf of @xmath150 and @xmath151 ; these @xmath152 plots show a characteristic , tear - drop shape .",
    "we explore the forms of these and other joint pdfs , such as joint pdfs of @xmath69 and @xmath70 , in mhd turbulence .",

    "pressure spectra have been studied for fluid turbulence as , e.g. , in refs .",
    "@xcite ; to the best of our knowledge they have not been obtained for mhd turbulence . the compensated spectra here show that , for all our runs , the inertial - range behaviours of these effective - pressure spectra are consistent with the power law @xmath178 ; this is consistent with the @xmath174 behaviours of the energy spectra discussed above .",
    "furthermore , as @xmath1 increases from @xmath269 to @xmath95 in runs r1-r5 , @xmath176 falls more and more rapidly as can be seen from the vertical scales in figs .",

    "we calculate several pdfs to characterise the statistical properties of decaying and statistically steady mhd turbulence . in the former case ,",
    "pdfs are obtained at the cascade - completion time @xmath45 ; in the latter , they are averaged over the statistically steady state that we obtain .",
    "the pdfs we consider are of two types : the first type are pdfs of the cosines of angles between various vectors , such as @xmath25 and @xmath141 ; these help us to quantify the degrees of alignment between such vectors ; the second type are pdfs of quantities such as @xmath69 , @xmath70 , and the eigenvalues of the rate - of - strain tensor .    in fig .",
    "[ fig : angle - w - eu ] we show plots of the pdfs of cosines of the angles between the vorticity @xmath141 and the eigenvectors of the fluid rate - of - strain tensor @xmath180 , namely , @xmath270 ( red full line ) , @xmath271 ( green dashed lines ) , and @xmath272 ( blue dotted lines ) for runs r1-r5 and r3b - r5b at the cascade - completion time @xmath45 for the case of decaying mhd turbulence . in fig .",
    "[ fig : angle - j - eu ] we show similar plots of the pdfs of cosines of the angles between the current density @xmath273 and the eigenvectors of the fluid rate - of - strain tensor @xmath180 .",
    "the most important features of these figures are sharp peaks in the green dashed lines ; these show that there is a marked tendency for the alignment or antialignment of @xmath141 and @xmath271 , as in fluid turbulence , and of a similar tendency for the alignment or antialignment of @xmath273 and @xmath274 ; these features do not depend very sensitively on @xmath1 .",
    "furthermore , the pdfs of cosines of the angles between @xmath141 and @xmath275 ( blue dotted lines ) and @xmath141 and @xmath272 ( red full lines ) show peaks near zero in fig .  [",
    "fig : angle - w - eu ] ; in contrast , analogous pdfs for the cosines of the angles between @xmath273 and @xmath270 ( red full lines ) and @xmath141 and @xmath272 ( blue dotted lines ) show nearly flat plateaux in the middle with very gentle maxima near @xmath276 and @xmath277 [ fig .",

    "all these pdfs have peaks close to @xmath291 ; this reflects the tendency for @xmath25 and @xmath26 to be aligned or antialigned that we have discussed above .",
    "however , these pdfs are quite broad and distinctly non - gaussian ; this can be seen easily from the values of the mean @xmath286 , standard deviation @xmath285 , skewness @xmath292 , and kurtosis @xmath293 given in table  [ table : hc ] .",
    "thus fluctuations of @xmath284 away from the mean are very significant .",
    "table  [ table : hc ] also gives the value of the mean energy @xmath170 and the ratio @xmath294 , which does not appear to be universal ; for the runs r1-r5 and r3b - r5b it lies in the range @xmath295-@xmath296 , for r1c - r2c in the range @xmath297-@xmath298 , and for r1d - r4d in the range @xmath299-@xmath300 .",
    "for all our runs , with the exception of r2c , the mean @xmath286 and the skewness @xmath292 are positive .",
    "even if the pdf of @xmath284 had been a gaussian , its mean value would have been within one standard deviation of 0 ; the actual pdf is much broader than a gaussian . on symmetry grounds",
    "there is no reason for the system to display a nonzero value for @xmath286 unless there is some bias in the forcing or in the initial condition ( the latter for the case of decaying turbulence ) . in any given run",
    ", if there is some residual @xmath284 , it is reflected in a slight asymmetry in alignment ( or antialignment ) of @xmath25 and @xmath26 , which we have studied above via the pdf of the cosine of the angle between @xmath25 and @xmath26 .",
    "when we consider the ratio @xmath289 it seems to be substantial in some runs but , given the arguments above , we expect it to vanish in runs with a very large number of collocation points ; indeed , it is very small in runs r1c - r4c .",

    "the pdfs of velocity increments are shown for separations @xmath347 ( red dashed thin line ) , @xmath348 ( green dot - dashed thin line ) , and @xmath349 ( blue full thin line ) , where @xmath350 is our real - space lattice spacing ; for pdfs of magnetic - field increments we also use the separations @xmath338 ( black dashed line ) , @xmath351 ( cyan dot - dashed line ) , and @xmath352 ( magenta full line ) ; the arguments of these pdfs are scaled by their standard deviations . as in fluid turbulence , we see that these pdfs are nearly gaussian if the length scale @xmath159 is large . as @xmath159 decreases ,",
    "the pdfs develop , long , non - gaussian tails , a clear signature of intermittency .",
    "furthermore , a comparison of the red and black dashed lines in these plots indicates that the pdfs of the magnetic - field increments are broader than their velocity counterparts in most of our runs ; this suggests , as we had surmised from the pdfs of energy - dissipation rates given above , that the magnetic field displays stronger intermittency than the velocity field at all but the smallest values of @xmath1 [ figs .",
    "[ fig : incrementpdfs](a.1 ) , [ fig : incrementpdfs](a.2 ) , and [ fig : incrementpdfs](a.3 ) for runs r1 , r1c , and r1d ] ; the general trend that we notice from these figures is that the magnetic - field intermittency is stronger than that of the velocity field at large magnetic prandtl numbers but the difference between these intermittencies decreases as @xmath1 is lowered .",
    "we will try to quantify this when we present structure functions in subsection  [ sec : stfn ] .",

    "[ fig : stfn-1024](a.2)-[fig : stfn-1024](d.2 ) ; the local slopes of these ess curves are shown in the insets of these figures .",
    "flat portions in these plots of local slopes help us to identify the inertial ranges .",
    "the regions that we have chosen for our fits are indicated by black horizontal lines with vertical ticks at their ends .",
    "in such a region , the mean value and the standard deviation of the local slope of the ess plot for @xmath393 ( or @xmath394 ) yield , respectively , our estimates for the exponent ratio @xmath363 ( or @xmath364 ) and its errorbars . figures  [ fig : stfn-1024](a.3)-[fig : stfn-1024](d.3 ) show plots of these exponent ratios versus @xmath32 for the velocity field ( blue dotted line with thick errorbars ) and the magnetic field ( red dashed line with thin error bars ) ; the black solid line shows the k41 result for comparison . though earlier studies  @xcite have obtained such exponents from dns studies , they have done so , to the best of our knowledge , only for @xmath395 ; furthermore , they have not reported errorbars .",
    "although our ( conservative ) errorbars are large , our plots of exponent ratios suggest the following : ( a ) deviations from the k41 result are significant , especially for @xmath203 , as in fluid turbulence ; ( b ) at large values of @xmath1 the magnetic field is more intermittent than the velocity field , in so far as the deviations of @xmath364 from the k41 result @xmath396 are larger than those of @xmath363 ; ( c ) as we reduce @xmath1 this difference in intermittency reduces until , at @xmath397 , the velocity field shows signs of becoming more intermittent than the magnetic field .",
    "this trend in intermittency is corroborated by plots versus @xmath159 of the the hyperflatnesses @xmath398 ( red line ) and @xmath399 ( blue dashed line ) in figs .",
    "[ fig : stfn-1024](a.4)-[fig : stfn-1024](d.4 ) for runs r1c - r4c , respectively : as @xmath159 decreases , @xmath385 rises more rapidly than @xmath384 except at @xmath397 .",

    "but , if we make up for the increase in @xmath7 by increasing the initial energy or @xmath44 so that @xmath262 and @xmath308 are both @xmath309 , we see that the tails of the pdfs get elongated again .",
    "we have carried out an extensive study of the statistical properties of both decaying and statistically steady homogeneous , isotropic mhd turbulence .",
    "our study , which has been designed specifically to study the systematics of the dependence of these properties on the magnetic prandtl number @xmath1 , uses a large number of statistical measures to characterise the statistical properties of both decaying and statistically steady mhd turbulence .",
    "our study is restricted to incompressible mhd turbulence ; we do not include a mean magnetic field as , e.g. , in refs .",
    "@xcite ; furthermore we do not study lagrangian properties considered , e.g. , in ref .",
    "@xcite . in our studies",
    "we obtain ( a ) various pdfs , such as those of the moduli of the vorticity and current density , the energy dissipation rates , of cosines of angles between various vectors , and scale - dependent velocity and magnetic - field increments , ( b ) spectra , e.g. , those of the energy and the effective pressure , ( c ) velocity and magnetic - field structure functions that can be used to characterise intermittency , ( d ) isosurfaces of quantities such as the moduli of the vorticity and current , and ( e ) joint pdfs such as @xmath152 plots .",
    "the evolution of these properties with @xmath23 has been described in detail in the previous section .    to the best of our knowledge ,",
    "such a comprehensive study of the @xmath410dependence of incompressible , homogeneous , isotropic mhd turbulence , both decaying and statistically steady , has not been attempted before .",
    "studies that draw their inspiration from astrophysics often consider anisotropic flows  @xcite , flows that are compressible  @xcite , or flows that include a mean magnetic field  @xcite .",
    "yet other studies concentrate on the alignment between various vectors such as @xmath25 and @xmath26 as , e.g. , in refs .",
    "@xcite ; some of these include a few , but not all , of the pdfs we have studied ; and , typically , these studies are restricted to the case @xmath22 .",
    "some of the spectra we study have been obtained in earlier dns studies but , typically , only for the case @xmath395 ; a notable exception is ref .",
    "@xcite , which examines the @xmath410dependence of energy spectra but with a relatively low resolution .",
    "references  @xcite have also considered some @xmath411dependence but not for low @xmath1 .",
    "isosurfaces of the moduli of the vorticity and current density have been obtained earlier  @xcite for the case @xmath22 .",
    "the @xmath1 dependence of these and other isosurfaces is presented here for the first time .",
    "the joint pdfs we have shown above have also not been investigated before .    here",
    "we wish to highlight , and examine in detail , the implications of our study for intermittency . some earlier dns studies , such as refs .",
    "@xcite , had noted that , for the case @xmath22 , the magnetic field is more intermittent than the velocity field .",
    "this is why we have concentrated on velocity and magnetic - field structure functions .",
    "our study confirms this finding , for the case @xmath22 .",
    "this can be seen clearly from the comparison of our exponent ratios , for @xmath22 , with those of the recent dns of decaying - mhd - turbulence in ref .",
    "@xcite in table  [ table : compare ] ; the errorbars that we quote for our exponent ratios have been calculated as described in the previous section ; we have obtained exponent ratios for ref .",
    "@xcite by digitising  @xcite the data in their plot [ fig .  3 of ref .",
    "@xcite ] of multiscaling exponents versus the order @xmath32 ( error bars are not given in their plot ) .",
    "thus , at least given our errorbars , there is agreement between our exponent ratios , both for decaying and statistically steady mhd turbulence , and those of ref .",
    "@xcite for @xmath22 .",
    "we note in passing that the latter dns is one of decaying mhd turbulence but with a very special initial condition , which allows an effective resolution greater than that we have obtained ; however , the initial condition we use in our decaying - mhd - turbulence dns is more generic than that of ref .",
    "it is our expectation that nonuniversal effects , associated with different initial conditions  @xcite , might not affect multiscaling exponent ratios , except if we use nongeneric , power - law initial conditions  @xcite in which @xmath172 grows with @xmath101 ( at least until some large-@xmath101 cutoff ) .",
    "direct numerical simulations of decaying - mhd - turbulence , e.g. , those of refs .",
    "@xcite , often average data obtained from field configurations at different times that are close to the time at which the peak appears in plots of the energy - dissipation rate .",
    "this is a reasonable procedure , for @xmath22 , because the temporal evolution of the system is slow in the vicinity of this peak .",
    "we have not adopted this procedure here because , as we move away from @xmath22 , the cascade - completion peaks occur at different times in plots of @xmath69 and @xmath70 as we have discussed in detail in earlier sections of this paper .",
    "let us now turn to the @xmath411dependence of the multiscaling exponent ratios shown in tables  [ table : zetap - decaying ] and [ table : zetap - forced ] and in figs.[fig : stfn-1024](a.3)-[fig : stfn-1024](d.3 ) and [ fig : stfn - forced](a.3)-[fig : stfn - forced](d.3 ) .",
    "even though our error bars are large , given the conservative , local - slope error analysis we have described in the previous section , a trend emerges : at large values of @xmath1 the magnetic field is clearly more intermittent than the velocity field , in as much as the deviations of @xmath361 from the simple - scaling prediction are stronger than their counterparts for @xmath206 .",
    "however , the velocity field becomes more intermittent than the magnetic field as we lower @xmath1 .",
    "could this result , namely , the dependence of our multiscaling exponent ratios on @xmath1 , be an artifact ?",
    "we believe not .",
    "as we have discussed above , dissipation ranges in our spectra are adequately resolved ; furthermore , we have determined exponent ratios from a a rather stringent local - slope analysis , which is rarely presented in earlier dns studies of mhd turbulence .",
    "ultimately , of course , this @xmath23 dependence of multiscaling exponents in mhd turbulence must be tested in detail in very - high - resolution dns studies of mhd turbulence ; such studies should become possible with the next generation of supercomputers .",
    "it is useful to note at this stage that a recent experimental study of mhd turbulence in the solar wind  @xcite provides evidence for velocity fields that are more strongly intermittent than the magnetic field ; this study does not give the value of @xmath1 .",
    "however , their data for multiscaling exponents are qualitatively similar to those we obtain at low values of @xmath1 .",
    "furthermore , pdfs of @xmath284 have also been obtained from solar - wind data  @xcite ; these are similar to the pdfs we obtain for @xmath284 . of course",
    ", we must exercise caution in comparing results from dns studies of homogeneous , isotropic , incompressible mhd turbulence with measurements on the solar wind where anisotropy and compressibility can be significant ; and , for the solar wind , we might also have to consider kinetic effects that are not captured by the mhd equations .",
    "the last point we wish to address is the issue of strong universality of exponent ratios . in the fluid - turbulence context",
    "such strong universality  @xcite implies the equality of exponents ( and , therefore , their ratios ) determined from decaying - turbulence studies ( say at the cascade - completion time ) or from studies of statistically steady turbulence .",
    "does such strong universality have an analogue in mhd turbulence ?",
    "our data , for any fixed value of @xmath1 in tables  [ table : zetap - decaying ] and [ table : zetap - forced ] , are consistent with such strong universality of multiscaling exponent ratios in mhd turbulence ; but , of course , our large errorbars imply that a definitive confirmation of such strong universality in mhd turbulence must await dns studies that might become possible in the next generation of high - performance - computing facilities .",

  "abstract_text": [
    "<S> we present the results of our detailed pseudospectral direct numerical simulation ( dns ) studies , with up to @xmath0 collocation points , of incompressible , magnetohydrodynamic ( mhd ) turbulence in three dimensions , without a mean magnetic field . </S>",
    "<S> our study concentrates on the dependence of various statistical properties of both decaying and statistically steady mhd turbulence on the magnetic prandtl number @xmath1 over a large range , namely , @xmath2 . </S>",
    "<S> we obtain data for a wide variety of statistical measures such as probability distribution functions ( pdfs ) of moduli of the vorticity and current density , the energy dissipation rates , and velocity and magnetic - field increments , energy and other spectra , velocity and magnetic - field structure functions , which we use to characterise intermittency , isosurfaces of quantities such as the moduli of the vorticity and current , and joint pdfs such as those of fluid and magnetic dissipation rates . </S>",
    "<S> our systematic study uncovers interesting results that have not been noted hitherto . </S>",
    "<S> in particular , we find a crossover from larger intermittency in the magnetic field than in the velocity field , at large @xmath1 , to smaller intermittency in the magnetic field than in the velocity field , at low @xmath1 . </S>",
    "<S> furthermore , a comparison of our results for decaying mhd turbulence and its forced , statistically steady analogue suggests that we have strong universality in the sense that , for a fixed value of @xmath1 , multiscaling exponent ratios agree , at least within our errorbars , for both decaying and statistically steady homogeneous , isotropic mhd turbulence . </S>"
